Actor RSocks (aka Stanx, Secrets_Line, SecretsLine) advertises SOCKS, VPN provider rsocks.net; Service reviewed, linked to RUSdot forum administrators; Front-end proxies revealed

04 May 2018 19:34:43 UTC
{ "tab": "raw" } Raw text { "tab": "comments" } Researcher comments

[source: https://titan.intel471.com/post_thread/fd94398286a6856e588cdc5f09e9f9c9?post_uid=2ae7f19f36e373e825680872e05c193e ]

Assessment of credibility

Intel471's database reveals the rsocks.net service has been offered in the underground since at least 2015, when the actor RSocks posted an advertisement thread for the "RUSdot Socks Server" on the exploit.in forum June 29, 2015. On the same thread, the actor claimed the service had the support of the RUSdot.com forum which we previously reported as a spam discussion board operated by the actor Stanx (see: Similar Reports section). Our database also reveals another thread posted by the actor Stanx on the exploit.in forum for the rsocks.net service (see: https://titan.intel471.com/post_thread/e01290b336e1f74ef6b8bece40ac4476?post_uid=a02feabf224a1d368f2bd4605d6e41d6 ), confirming the link between this actor and the socket secure (SOCKS) service. Further research using our database shows the actor is active on several underground forums where he collected a number of positive feedback posts. Considering the long-term positive reputation for the service, we assess this information with the Credibility of "2 — Probably True."

The actor offered the email address support@rsocks.net, Jabber ID support@rsocks.net, Telegram @RSocks, Skype name rsocks.net, QQ 3307018252 and ICQ ID 560335 for direct communication. Our sensitive source used the actor's Jabber ID to ask for a free test as advertised and received a two-hour access to one of the service’s subscription plans to review the control panel.

 

Overview of the rsocks.net service

The service offers the following products:

— Standard proxy: This option offers general purpose, non-exclusive hyptertext transfer protocol (HTTP), secure HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS4a and SOCKS5 proxies. The actor claims all ports are open and the list of available proxies is updated every two hours with up to 30 percent of the new proxies in each update, which can give more than 90,000 IP addresses per day depending on the contract package. Prices ranges from US $5 for an hourly access to the "World Mix 1" package to US $4,000 for a one-month subscription to the "World Mix 10." Packages differ on the number of available proxies for use. The actor claimed "World Mix" has 9,000 IP addresses and "World Mix 10" has more than 90,000 available proxies for use. The service offers intermediate options and geolocated plans with IP addresses from China, Commonwealth of Independent States (CIS) countries, Europe and the U.S. The actor claims proxy lists are cleaned daily using the Spamhaus Project databases.

— Exclusive proxy: These have the same characteristics of standard proxies, but they are issued exclusively per client and operate at higher speeds. The exclusive proxy package contains between 4,000 and 40,000 ports. Prices range from US $50 for a daily access to "Exclusive Mix 1" with at least 4,000 IP addresses to US $12,000 for a one-month access to the "Exclusive Mix 10" with 40,000 IP addresses.

— Platinum proxy: According to the service description, the Platinum proxies execute on a new, improved kernel based on a SOCKS5 protocol. These proxies are not included on any blacklists and are intended exclusively for white projects. The actor claims all non-working IP address updates for one minute maintain a permanent online presence of the whole package. Ports 25, 465 and 587 are closed and do not allow users to work through these proxies, reducing the risk of IP addresses being added to blacklists. These optional packages are given only to trusted and reliable customers, in a narrowly limited number. Prices range from US $30 for a one-day access to the "Platinum RU" plan with 1,000 Russian IP addresses to US $800 for a one-month subscription to the "Platinum Mix" plan with 2,000 IP addresses.

— Personal proxy: These proxy IP addresses are issued exclusively per client. Price is US $5 per IP address per month.

—  Server proxies: Similar to personal proxies, a proxy IP address is issued exclusively per client, the server package offers as many as 8,000 IP addresses restricted to white projects only. At this time, this package only is available for U.S. IP addresses with prices ranging from US $70 to $500, per week or per month, respectively.

— VPN Service: This option offers virtual private network (VPN) plans with geolocated servers, supporting the point-to-point tunneling protocol (PPTP), internet protocol security (IPsec) and VPN with Tor, with single- or double-chain nodes. This service supports the OpenVPN software client, although the actor also offers his private client downloads for Android, Mac and Windows. Prices range from US $10 for a monthly subscription to a single-node VPN plan to US $180 for a year of VPN with Tor package. At the time of this report, the actor offered the following VPN servers IP addresses:

Open source research

The domain rsocks.net was registered using a privacy protection company. At this time, the domain resolves to the IP address 5.45.70.26 (Netherlands — Serverius Holding B.V.) According to passive domain name system (DNS) research, the same IP address also resolves to the following domains:

— rsocks.info: Alternative domain for the service, registered using the email address petr.iv99@bk.ru of an individual named Petr Ivanov.
— rsocks.org: Another alternative domain for the rsocks.net service and the domain also was registered with the email petr.iv99@bk.ru.
— stanx.ru: This domain points to a simple webpage with the text "Contacts" and the information ICQ 399611, Jabber ID stanx@rusdot.com and email address istanx@gmail.com. Our database reveals the actor Stanx registered at the Damagelab forum using this email address. An actor using the moniker bzeek registered at the Antichat forum using the ICQ 399611 and email address bzeek@mail.ru. This domain has 136 subdomains, including instagram.stanx.ru and hotmail.stanx.ru, which most likely are used for phishing attacks. The subdomain dk.stanx.ru redirects to the Instagram page https://www.instagram.com/deniskloster/ of an individual named Denis Kloster and reveals the domain deniskloster.com. In our previous report on the actor Stanx, we already discovered a link between the actor and this individual. The Google profile linked to the email address istanx@gmail.com displays the image of the same individual pictured on this Instagram account. The subdomain job.stanx.ru redirects to http://job.exelo.ru, which is a Cost Per Action (CPA) advertising network named Exelo Media. At this time, it is unclear whether the actor also is behind Exelo Media or is just an affiliate, although the domain exelo.ru server redirected to exploit kit (EK) landing pages in the past (see: https://www.malware-traffic-analysis.net/2014/05/23/index2.htm ).
— rsocks.biz: Alternative domain also registered using the email address petr.iv99@bk.ru. The WHOIS records also reveal the phone number 447937967334.
— rsocks.de: This is another alternative domain.
— rsocks.es: The Spanish-language version of the rsocks.net service website.
— r-socks.cn: The Chinese version of the rsocks.net service website.
— secretsline.biz: This domain hosts the SecretsLine VPN service provider website. This provider offers VPN packages with a description similar to rsocks.net and operates under the same control panel platform engine. A private VPN client application also is offered to Android, Mac and Windows systems. Our database reveals an actor using the monikers Secrets_Line and SecretsLine posted advertisement threads for this service on several underground forums, where he offered the email address support@secretsline.biz, Jabber ID support@secretsline.biz, Skype name secretsline.biz, Telegram ID @secretsline and ICQ UIN 444555 for direct communication and the alternative domain secretsline.org. The actor SecretsLine offered the phone number 447937977645, which also was used by the actor RSocks in an advertisement thread on the searchengines.guru forum (see: hxxps://searchengines[.]guru/showthread.php?t=970156 ). His account on this forum also is linked to https://twitter.com/rsocksnet.

The secretsline.biz site has been advertised since at least 2007, by the actor secreTSline. In a post on the Prologic forum May 27, 2008, the actor said he was arrested and his service no longer could be trusted. Shortly after thereafter, he continued business as usual (see: https://titan.intel471.com/post_thread/0ecfeb6e2b3bbfa6f1f85dd6add793e0 ).

 

The actor's other activity on underground

Intel 471's database reveals a number of actors using the monikers Stanx or RSocks on several underground forums, including major Russian-language boards. Our research indicates the actor primarily is focused on promoting and discussing his service, answering questions and responding to support issues. A Titan search provides a complete list of actors and forums where he is present (see: https://titan.intel471.com/search/Actor:RSOCKS%20%7C%7C%20Stanx/reports?ordering=latest ).

 

Partial description of the rsocks.net infrastructure

Our source captured some information on the actor's infrastructure. This information should not be considered definitive or complete, but just a sample snapshot, since the actor appears to have a very large and distributed operation.

When an rsocks.net service user buys a plan, it must be activated for a single source IP address representing the user's IP address which will be connecting to the proxies. An option for adding more source IP addresses to this white list is available for an extra charge of 50 percent of package's price per additional IP address. After setting the source IP address, the package rental period can be started and paused a number of times, depending on the plan, but daily or hourly packages cannot be paused. The service permits using the acquired pool of proxies during the period, switching a fraction of proxies within the pool every two hours. Twenty-four hours later, the user can manually switch the entire pool of addresses for new ones. 

The proxy pool available for the users can be downloaded from the service control panel as a text file in the format IP:PORT, where IP is the back-end or entry node proxy and PORT is the transmission control protocol (TCP) port. When connecting to an IP:PORT from this list, the user is redirected to a front-end or exit node proxy before reaching his final destination on internet. The control panel offers no option to identify the exit node IP address or its geolocation before purchase. A client application named "RSocks Proxy Checker" is available for Linux, macOS and Windows, allowing the user to load the proxy list into the application and perform filtering based on geolocation, proxy response speed, if address is blacklisted or not and check the exit node real IP address and host name, if available.
